# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Firefox SpiderMonkey JS Parsing to Bytecode Chain

## Your Task

Trace how JavaScript source text is parsed and compiled to bytecode in mozilla/gecko-dev SpiderMonkey. Find C++ source files implementing: the JS parser entry point, the AST node types, the bytecode emitter, and the JSScript bytecode output.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/firefox--871325b8.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/firefox--871325b8` (mozilla-firefox/firefox)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

## Summary

I've created a comprehensive answer at `/workspace/answer.json` that documents the complete JavaScript parsing to bytecode compilation chain in Mozilla's SpiderMonkey engine. The document includes:

### **Key Components Found:**

1. **Entry Point**: `CompileGlobalScript()` in `BytecodeCompiler.h` - the high-level API for script compilation

2. **Compilation Pipeline**:
   - `CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate()` - sets up compilation state
   - `ScriptCompiler<Unit>::compile()` - orchestrates parsing and bytecode generation

3. **Parser Entry**: `Parser::globalBody()` and `Parser::evalBody()` - convert source to Abstract Syntax Tree

4. **AST Node Types** (in `ParseNode.h`):
   - Base `ParseNode` class (line 712)
   - `UnaryNode` (line 952) - unary operations
   - `BinaryNode` (line 1017) - binary operations  
   - `TernaryNode` (line 1115) - ternary operators
   - `ListNode` (line 1184) - statement/expression lists

5. **Bytecode Generation**: `BytecodeEmitter::emitScript()` (line 2354) - converts AST to bytecode instructions

6. **Bytecode Output**: `JSScript` class in `js/src/vm/JSScript.h` (line 1787) - the final bytecode container with `code()` method providing access to the bytecode array

The answer document includes all relevant files, symbols, the complete compilation chain, and a detailed narrative explaining how JavaScript source text flows through parsing, AST generation, and bytecode emission to produce executable SpiderMonkey bytecode.

It calls the parser, bytecode emitter, etc.\n36:  *\n37:  * ParseContext.h and SharedContext.h: Both have similar purposes. They're split\n38:  * because ParseContext contains information used only by the parser, and\n39:  * SharedContext contains information used by both the parser and\n40:  * BytecodeEmitter.\n41:  *\n42:  * SharedContext.h: class Directives: this contains boolean flags for tracking\n43:  * if we're in asm.js or \"use strict\" code. The \"use strict\" bit is stored in\n44:  * SharedContext, and additionally, the full Directives class is stored in\n45:  * ParseContext - if a direcive is encountered while parsing, this is updated,\n46:  * and checked in GeneralParser::functionDefinition, and if it changed, the\n47:  * whole function is re-parsed with the new flags.\n48:  *\n49:  * SharedContext.h: abstract class SharedContext: This class contains two\n50:  * different groups of flags:\n51:  *\n52:  * Parse context information. This is information conceptually \"passed down\"\n53:  * into parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"are we parsing strict code?\", and so\n54:  * the parser can make decisions of how to parse based off that.\n55:  *\n56:  * Gathered-while-parsing information. This is information conceptually\n57:  * \"returned up\" from parsing sub-nodes. This is like \"did we see a use strict\n58:  * directive\"?\n59:  *\n60:  * Additionally, subclasses (GlobalSharedContext, ModuleSharedContext,\n61:  * EvalSharedContext, and FunctionBox) contain binding information, scope\n62:  * information, and other such bits of data.\n63:  *\n64:  * ParseContext.h: class UsedNameTracker: Track which bindings are used in which\n65:  * scopes. This helps determine which bindings are closed-over, which affects\n66:  * how they're stored; and whether special bindings like `this` and `arguments`\n67:  * can be optimized away.\n68:  *\n69:  * ParseContext.h: class ParseContext: Extremely complex class that serves a lot\n70:  * of purposes, but it's a single class - essentially no derived classes - so\n71:  * it's a little easier to comprehend all at once. (SourceParseContext does\n72:  * derive from ParseContext, but they does nothing except adjust the\n73:  * constructor's arguments).\n74:  * Note it uses a thing called Nestable, which implements a stack of objects:\n75:  * you can push (and pop) instances to a stack (linked list) as you parse\n76:  * further into the parse tree. You may push to this stack via calling the\n77:  * constructor with a GeneralParser as an argument (usually `this`), which\n78:  * pushes itself onto `this->pc` (so it does get assigned/pushed, even though no\n79:  * assignment ever appears directly in the parser)\n80:  *\n81:  * ParseContext contains a pointer to a SharedContext.\n82:  *\n83:  * There's a decent chunk of flags/data collection in here too, some \"pass-down\"\n84:  * data and some \"return-up\" data.\n85:  *\n86:  * ParseContext also contains a significant number of *sub*-Nestables as fields\n87:  * of itself (nestables inside nestables). Note you also push/pop to these via\n88:  * passing `Parser->pc`, which the constructor of the sub-nestable knows which\n89:  * ParseContext field to push to. The sub-nestables are:\n90:  *\n91:  * ParseContext::Statement: stack of statements.\n92:  * `if (x) { while (true) { try { ..stack of [if, while, try].. } ... } }`\n93:  *\n94:  * ParseContext::LabelStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for labeled\n95:  * statements, for e.g. `label: while (true) { break label; }`\n96:  *\n97:  * ParseContext::ClassStatement: interspersed in Statement stack, for classes\n98:  * the parser is currently inside of.\n99:  *\n100:  * ParseContext::Scope: Set of variables in each scope (stack of sets):\n101:  * `{ let a; let b; { let c; } }`\n102:  * (this gets complicated with `var`, etc., check the class for docs)\n103:  */\n104: \n105: class JSFunction;\n106: class JSObject;\n107: class JSScript;\n108: struct The ScriptCompiler extends `SourceAwareCompiler` and orchestrates the entire compilation pipeline.\\n\\n## Parser Entry Points: globalBody and evalBody\\nIn `ScriptCompiler::compile()` (line 955 of BytecodeCompiler.cpp), the parser is invoked:\\n- For global scripts: `parser->globalBody(sc->asGlobalContext())` (line 977)\\n- For eval scripts: `parser->evalBody(sc->asEvalContext())` (line 975)\\n\\nThese methods are defined in `js/src/frontend/Parser.h` in the Parser class (line 1679), which is templatized along the ParseHandler axis (FullParseHandler for full parsing, SyntaxParseHandler for syntax-only parsing) and the Unit axis (character type). The parser converts JavaScript source text into an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) composed of ParseNode objects.\\n\\n## AST Node Types: ParseNode Hierarchy\\nThe AST nodes are defined in `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and include:\\n\\n- **ParseNode** (line 712): Base class for all AST nodes, identified by ParseNodeKind enum. Contains position information (pn_pos), type information (pn_type), and intrinsic links (pn_next).\\n- **UnaryNode** (line 952): Represents unary operations with a single child node (e.g., `!x`, `-y`, `typeof x`)\\n- **BinaryNode** (line 1017): Represents binary operations with left and right child nodes (e.g., `x + y`, `x && y`, `x = y`)\\n- **TernaryNode** (line 1115): Represents ternary conditional operations with three child nodes (e.g., `x ? y : z`)\\n- **ListNode** (line 1184): Represents lists of nodes for statements and expressions (e.g., statement lists, function arguments)\\n- Specialized nodes: **NameNode**, **NumericLiteral**, **StringExpr**, **FunctionNode**, **AssignmentNode**, **ForNode**, **ClassNames**, **ClassMethod**, etc.\\n\\nEach node type implements a `test()` static method for type checking via pattern matching.\\n\\n## Bytecode Emitter: Generating Bytecode\\nAfter successful parsing, `ScriptCompiler::compile()` creates a `BytecodeEmitter` (line 1004) and calls `emitter->emitScript(pn)` (line 1009) to emit bytecode from the AST.\\n\\nThe BytecodeEmitter is defined in `js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h` (line 210) and includes:\\n\\n- Constructor that receives the Parser, SharedContext, and CompilationState (lines 341-350)\\n- The `emitScript()` function (BytecodeEmitter.cpp, line 2354) is the entry point for emitting script bytecode\\n- Helper classes like ClassEmitter, PropertyEmitter, CallOrNewEmitter for specific constructs\\n- Separate prologue and main bytecode sections (lines 96-98 of BytecodeEmitter.h)\\n- Methods to emit individual bytecode instructions corresponding to AST nodes\\n\\n## Bytecode Output: JSScript\\nThe final bytecode is stored in a JSScript object, defined in `js/src/vm/JSScript.h` (line 1787). Key methods:\\n\\n- `JSScript::Create()` (line 1800): Creates a JSScript instance\\n- `JSScript::fullyInitFromStencil()` (line 1818): Initializes JSScript from the compilation stencil\\n- `JSScript::fromStencil()` (line 1826): Allocates and initializes a JSScript with bytecode\\n- `code()` (line 1844): Returns pointer to the bytecode array (`jsbytecode*`), which is an array of uint8_t values representing bytecode instructions\\n- `immutableScriptData()` (line 1839): Returns the immutable script data containing the bytecode\\n\\nThe bytecode can be navigated using `BytecodeLocation` (`js/src/vm/BytecodeLocation.h`) which provides utilities for working with bytecode positions within a JSScript.\\n\\n## Complete Data Flow\\nJavaScript source text \u2192 CompileGlobalScript() \u2192 CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate() \u2192 ScriptCompiler<Unit>::compile() \u2192 Parser::globalBody() \u2192 ParseNode AST \u2192 BytecodeEmitter::emitScript() \u2192 Bytecode instructions \u2192 JSScript with immutable bytecode array\\n\\nThis modular pipeline allows for lazy compilation of inner functions, separate parsing and bytecode generation phases, and optimization opportunities at each stage.\"",

The ScriptCompiler extends `SourceAwareCompiler` and orchestrates the entire compilation pipeline.\\n\\n## Parser Entry Points: globalBody and evalBody\\nIn `ScriptCompiler::compile()` (line 955 of BytecodeCompiler.cpp), the parser is invoked:\\n- For global scripts: `parser->globalBody(sc->asGlobalContext())` (line 977)\\n- For eval scripts: `parser->evalBody(sc->asEvalContext())` (line 975)\\n\\nThese methods are defined in `js/src/frontend/Parser.h` in the Parser class (line 1679), which is templatized along the ParseHandler axis (FullParseHandler for full parsing, SyntaxParseHandler for syntax-only parsing) and the Unit axis (character type). The parser converts JavaScript source text into an Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) composed of ParseNode objects.\\n\\n## AST Node Types: ParseNode Hierarchy\\nThe AST nodes are defined in `js/src/frontend/ParseNode.h` and include:\\n\\n- **ParseNode** (line 712): Base class for all AST nodes, identified by ParseNodeKind enum. Contains position information (pn_pos), type information (pn_type), and intrinsic links (pn_next).\\n- **UnaryNode** (line 952): Represents unary operations with a single child node (e.g., `!x`, `-y`, `typeof x`)\\n- **BinaryNode** (line 1017): Represents binary operations with left and right child nodes (e.g., `x + y`, `x && y`, `x = y`)\\n- **TernaryNode** (line 1115): Represents ternary conditional operations with three child nodes (e.g., `x ? y : z`)\\n- **ListNode** (line 1184): Represents lists of nodes for statements and expressions (e.g., statement lists, function arguments)\\n- Specialized nodes: **NameNode**, **NumericLiteral**, **StringExpr**, **FunctionNode**, **AssignmentNode**, **ForNode**, **ClassNames**, **ClassMethod**, etc.\\n\\nEach node type implements a `test()` static method for type checking via pattern matching.\\n\\n## Bytecode Emitter: Generating Bytecode\\nAfter successful parsing, `ScriptCompiler::compile()` creates a `BytecodeEmitter` (line 1004) and calls `emitter->emitScript(pn)` (line 1009) to emit bytecode from the AST.\\n\\nThe BytecodeEmitter is defined in `js/src/frontend/BytecodeEmitter.h` (line 210) and includes:\\n\\n- Constructor that receives the Parser, SharedContext, and CompilationState (lines 341-350)\\n- The `emitScript()` function (BytecodeEmitter.cpp, line 2354) is the entry point for emitting script bytecode\\n- Helper classes like ClassEmitter, PropertyEmitter, CallOrNewEmitter for specific constructs\\n- Separate prologue and main bytecode sections (lines 96-98 of BytecodeEmitter.h)\\n- Methods to emit individual bytecode instructions corresponding to AST nodes\\n\\n## Bytecode Output: JSScript\\nThe final bytecode is stored in a JSScript object, defined in `js/src/vm/JSScript.h` (line 1787). Key methods:\\n\\n- `JSScript::Create()` (line 1800): Creates a JSScript instance\\n- `JSScript::fullyInitFromStencil()` (line 1818): Initializes JSScript from the compilation stencil\\n- `JSScript::fromStencil()` (line 1826): Allocates and initializes a JSScript with bytecode\\n- `code()` (line 1844): Returns pointer to the bytecode array (`jsbytecode*`), which is an array of uint8_t values representing bytecode instructions\\n- `immutableScriptData()` (line 1839): Returns the immutable script data containing the bytecode\\n\\nThe bytecode can be navigated using `BytecodeLocation` (`js/src/vm/BytecodeLocation.h`) which provides utilities for working with bytecode positions within a JSScript.\\n\\n## Complete Data Flow\\nJavaScript source text \u2192 CompileGlobalScript() \u2192 CompileGlobalScriptToStencilAndMaybeInstantiate() \u2192 ScriptCompiler<Unit>::compile() \u2192 Parser::globalBody() \u2192 ParseNode AST \u2192 BytecodeEmitter::emitScript() \u2192 Bytecode instructions \u2192 JSScript with immutable bytecode array\\n\\nThis modular pipeline allows for lazy compilation of inner functions, separate parsing and bytecode generation phases, and optimization opportunities at each stage.\"",
